  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_0990bfa8-9b0a-4abd-9502-9792115934e8'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);

      initializeSiwa();

  <span id="freeText12461757594395147797" style="display:none"><p> A hidden truth. <br /> Mortal enemies. <br /> Doomed love. </p><p>Marked as special at an early age, Jacinda knows her every move is watched. But she longs for freedom to make her own choices. When she breaks the most sacred tenet among her kind, she nearly pays with her life. Until a beautiful stranger saves her. A stranger who was sent to hunt those like her. For Jacinda is a draki, a descendant of dragons whose greatest defense is her secret ability to shift into human form. </p><p>Forced to flee into the mortal world with her family, Jacinda struggles to adapt to her new surroundings. The only bright light is Will. Gorgeous, elusive Will who stirs her inner draki to life. Although she is irresistibly drawn to him, Jacinda knows Will's dark secret: He and his family are hunters. She should avoid him at all costs. But her inner draki is slowly slipping away;if it dies she will be left as a human forever. She'll do anything to prevent that. Even if it means getting closer to her most dangerous enemy.</p> <p>Mythical powers and breathtaking romance ignite in this story of a girl who defies all expectations and whose love crosses an ancient divide.</p></span>

<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/9910579-becky"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1542680201i/9910579._UY100_CR16,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>

<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/9910579-becky">Becky</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I read both books within a few weeks of each other! They are very similar in terms of concept, pacing, and the main characters from both series are in<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I read both books within a few weeks of each other! They are very similar in terms of concept, pacing, and the main characters from both series are in love with a boy who is part of a group that hunts down their species. I often felt like I was reading the same book twice, though if I had to choose between which one I liked better, it would be Firelight. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_1471493023" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1471493023" />
    <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies"><img alt="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500999223p2/4527753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1471493023?book_show_action=true">Dec 17, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1471493023" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer578270002470632910"><blockquote>
  <i>His black T-shirt is a second skin, plastered to his lean chest. In our shadowed cave, his wet hair looks nearly black. It could be lighter when dry. Medium brown or even a dark blond. But it’s his eyes that hold me. Deeply set beneath thick brows, they drill into me with a stark intensity, scanning me, all of me.<br/><br/>In that single moment we connected. Somehow it happened.</i>
</blockquote><b>Oh, god save us all from insta-love.</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1450374858ra/17417795.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>The plot is dumb because the stupid little emo rhymes-with-itch main character, Jacinda, </b></span>
  <span id="freeText578270002470632910" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>His black T-shirt is a second skin, plastered to his lean chest. In our shadowed cave, his wet hair looks nearly black. It could be lighter when dry. Medium brown or even a dark blond. But it’s his eyes that hold me. Deeply set beneath thick brows, they drill into me with a stark intensity, scanning me, all of me.<br><br>In that single moment we connected. Somehow it happened.</i>
</blockquote><b>Oh, god save us all from insta-love.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1450374858ra/17417795.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>The plot is dumb because the stupid little emo rhymes-with-itch main character, Jacinda, is dumb as shit</b>. It essentially goes like this: special dragon-girl is special. She doesn't want to be special, but can't help it. She's practically engaged to the prince of her people because she's so special. She has to hide the fact that she's a dragon (because people kill dragons, more specifically, <b>Hunters</b> kill dragons). I guess dragon parts are like rhinoceros horns, they're aphrodisiac and shit, which is confusing because <b>whenever I read about Jacinda interacting with her insta-love, I don't feel turned on, I feel like puking</b>. Despite knowing she has to hide, Jacinda breaks the rules, turns into a dragon and flies at dawn because SHE WANTS TO FEEL THE SUNLIGHT ON HER SKIN (no, really, that's why she endangers her entire species). Her mom freaks out because she feels that her daughters are being raised in a dangerous cult and brings Jacinda and her non-dragon-turning twin sister Tamra into the Real World (not the MTV show). Tamra is happy. Jacinda is miserable and spends the rest of the book whining and being emo and a gigantic brat about how HER MOM'S RUINING HER LIFE. Like every single teenager ever. Oh, and she falls into insta-love with the one guy who's part of the <b>Hunters</b> (in case you guys don't remember, Hunters are the ones who want to kill all the dragons and chop them up for parts). <br><br>Brilliant, right?<br><br>In case you guys didn't get the drift from my introductory sentence, <b>this book was fucking terrible.</b> We've got the holy trifecta of YA idiocy. <b>Insta love</b> (see above), a speshul, speshul <b>Mary Sue</b> who's SO DIFFERENT AND UNIQUE AND RARE!<blockquote>
  <i>I breathe fire. The only fire-breather in the pride in more than four hundred years. It’s made me more popular than I want to be.</i>
</blockquote>Well, whaddya know, such a thing has never happened before in YA literature. Annnnnnnnnnd the final part in the holy trifecta of idiocy, <b>falling in love with your enemy</b>.<blockquote>
  <i>“Jace! You’re glowing!”<br>That jerks my attention back. I glance down at my arms. My skin blurs in and out, shimmering faintly, like I’ve been dusted with gold.<br>The draki in me stirs, tingling, yearning to come out.<br>“God, get a grip, jeez!” Tamra hisses, leaning closer. “You see a hot guy and start to manifest? Have some control.”</i>
</blockquote><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1450374858ra/17417796.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Who, is, of course, the most best wonderfulest most chastestest boy in the whole wide world who, naturally, remains completely pure and uncatchable until he *clasps my heart* sees her!!!1!one<blockquote>
  <i>“Well. Will…” A wistful smile curves her mouth. “He’s elusive. None of the girls here interest him.” She rolls her magnificent eyes and sighs dramatically. “Course that just makes us want him harder.”<br>Stupid delight flutters inside my chest.</i>
</blockquote>So original. So surprising.<br><br>But yeah. This book is dumb. Have I said that before? I might have. There's <b>so much fucking insta-love</b>.<blockquote>
  <i>But I still feel him. Yearn for him. Know he’s there even when I no longer see him.</i>
</blockquote>FOR FUCK'S SAKES, YOU KNEW HIM FOR 30 SECONDS. For the rest of the book, Will is mentioned CONSTANTLY. How dreamy he is. How much she thinks about him. Their secret, unknown, impossible connection!<blockquote>
  <i>His words echo inside me. You should stay away from me. Something I already know, but sitting in the front seat of his car, I’m not quite succeeding at that. I wish I could. Wish I didn’t feel this pull, this constant tug toward him. Wish my draki didn’t revive around him.</i>
</blockquote>Fuck me.<br><br>She does stupid shit to get herself in danger, like, oh, ALMOST SHOWING HER TRUE FORM AT HER HUMAN SCHOOL BECAUSE A BOY MADE HER PANTIES MOIST.<blockquote>
  <i>Even hunters don’t know draki manifest into human form. It’s been our most carefully guarded secret. Our greatest defense. And it’s not like I was unfurling my wings in the hallway. Not quite, anyway.</i>
</blockquote>Oh, right, she only <i>almost</i> did it. So much better. Falling in love with the enemy is such a conflicting thing, isn't it?<blockquote>
  <i>When it comes to Will, my feelings are terrible and confusing. To want him safely back one moment, but pray that whatever draki he hunts is safe and free in the next. The two wishes conflict.</i>
</blockquote><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1450374858i/17417797.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Will is so wonderful. So caring that he finds out where she lives without her knowledge.<blockquote>
  <i>“It’s not hard to find out. Your address is on file in the school office.”<br>“You broke into the school office?”<br>“No. I know one of the office aides. She got me your address that first day.”<br>My first day. He’s had my address all this time. </i>
</blockquote>So romantic! And there's nothing better than forbidden love. Especially forbidden love of which Jacinda reminds us every, oh, 15 seconds.<blockquote>
  <i>Every moment with Will, I feel at risk, exposed. Danger hangs close, as tangible as the heavy mists I’ve left behind. And I can’t get enough of it. Of him. I crave his nearness still. Like a drug needed to survive, to get by each day. An addiction. A powerful, consuming thing.</i>
</blockquote>The characters are so <b>one dimensional</b>. Jacinda really doesn't give a shit about anyone but her wish to be a dragon and Will. Her relationship with her twin sister is flat. She ignores her mom. The side characters, like the kids in school, are just stereotypical portrayals, the bitch, the jock, the creepers. The entire book revolves around Jacinda, and god help us if any one else gets their own moment in the spotlight. Every single girl is portrayed poorly. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1450374858ra/17417798.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Don't waste your time with this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="578270002470632910" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_105502587" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/105502587" />
    <a title="Shannon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2016128-shannon"><img alt="Shannon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572638169p2/2016128.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/105502587?book_show_action=true">Jun 03, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shannon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shannon" href="/user/show/2016128-shannon">Shannon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=color-red">color-red</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=dragons">dragons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=shifters">shifters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=terrible-writing">terrible-writing</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=2011">2011</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=borrowed">borrowed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=abandoned-series">abandoned-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2016128-shannon?shelf=dumb-female-characters">dumb-female-characters</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer105502587" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17692226510067834548"><b>Incredibly disappointed.</b> Those two words sum up my feelings for this book pretty succinctly. What could have been an awesome teen book with dragon shifters and the trials of wanting to fit in turned into a whine- and pine-fest the likes of which I’ve never seen before. (And no, I have <i>not</i> read Twilight.) <br/><br/><b>There aren’t any glaring spoilers in this review, at least nothing that couldn’t be gleaned from the dust jacket, but I do discuss most of the book here, so you’re forewarned!</b><br/><br/><i>Preemptive apology </i></span>
  <span id="freeText17692226510067834548" style="display:none"><b>Incredibly disappointed.</b> Those two words sum up my feelings for this book pretty succinctly. What could have been an awesome teen book with dragon shifters and the trials of wanting to fit in turned into a whine- and pine-fest the likes of which I’ve never seen before. (And no, I have <i>not</i> read Twilight.) <br /><br /><b>There aren’t any glaring spoilers in this review, at least nothing that couldn’t be gleaned from the dust jacket, but I do discuss most of the book here, so you’re forewarned!</b><br /><br /><i>Preemptive apology here – I realize this is a long review, but it’s #100 for me, and I felt the need to rant, so …</i><br /><br />Jacinda is a fire-breathing draki (dragon-like creature) who lives in a cultish commune with other draki. She’s sick of the rules, especially the ones designed to keep her safe, and so decides she just <i>has</i> to go flying during the day, when it’s quite possible that humans will see her. She goes out flying with her friend and of course they’re spotted by hunters. One hunter, a boy near Jacinda’s age, finds her trapped in a cave and decides to let her go and lead his hunter friends away. Although both girls make it back, Jacinda’s mother decides it no longer safe for Jacinda in the pride and takes off for the fictional desert town of Chaparral, 90 miles outside Las Vegas. <b>From here is where the book takes off in a ridiculous direction.</b><br /><br />Jacinda’s pride lives somewhere in the Cascade Mountains. Her mother takes her to Nevada to enroll in high school, hoping to “kill” Jacinda’s draki in the dry desert heat. Now I bet you’re thinking, between the Cascades and Nevada there’s probably more than one high school, right? Well then, what are the odds that the hunter who found Jacinda in the mountains is enrolled at the high school in Nevada? Well, this <i>is</i> a teen book we’re reading here, so of <i>course</i> the “beautiful” boy, Will, who saves Jacinda is also in the same grade in the same school, a few states away. <i>Totally</i> makes sense.<br /><br /><b>Ok, so maybe I can get over the coincidence that they’re attending the same school.</b> But still, Will is a hunter! Hunters kill and maim her people, selling them as meat and skin to the highest bidder. <b>And yet, she instantly falls head over heels in love with him.</b> And also, when she realizes he’s in the same school as her and her twin sister, she doesn’t warn her family! She doesn’t say, “hey, you remember just a week ago when I was running for my life from hunters? Well, at least one of them is enrolled in the same high school as us.” Yeah, don’t protect your flesh and blood because you don’t want your mom to pull you out of school and make you redo the “wretched first day all over again, suffering the heat and climate somewhere else without a beautiful, exciting boy around.” Seriously, are you kidding me? <b>You don’t want to keep yourself and your family safe because of some awkwardness and hormones?</b> This is beyond selfish.<br /><br />I started to count the amount of times that Jacinda would notice Will before she saw him. It gets ridiculous and this is just another instance of the author filling up the pages with more whining and pining. (Seriously, that should have been the name of this book.) <b>I get what she’s trying to establish; that Jacinda and Will’s relationship is something special that defies meaning, but the way she went about this was just cheesy and sappy.</b> Here’s what I came across that stuck out for me:<br /><blockquote>"I still feel him. Yearn for him. Know he's there even when I no longer see him." (51)<br />"My flesh pulls and tightens with awareness, and I know it's him before he enters the room." (56)<br />"And almost as if I've summoned him, I feel him arrive. My skin shivers, and the tiny hairs at my nape stand on end. Like in the hall today before I even saw him, but knew he was near." (73)<br />"That feeling comes over me again, and immediately I know he's here." (87)<br />"That much-missed vibration ignites in my chest, spreads to my core. My skin snaps alive. My head turns, eyes searching, honing in on Will as he walks into the room." (108)<br />"His presence always does this to me. Breathe life back in. Chases away the phantom like fast-fading mist. My skin tightens, rushes with awareness. My chest vibrates. Swells with relief, gratitude, and something else." (177)</blockquote><br /><b>It’s like every time Will enters a room he sets off some sort of motion sensor in Jacinda.</b> Why do they love each other? The only thing they have in common is being good-looking and an association with draki – they don’t know anything about each other and the only thing drawing them together is this physical attraction that the author has forced into being “love.”<br /><br /><b>A lot of Jacinda’s inner monologue makes absolutely no sense.</b> She’s constantly telling herself to stay away from Will, that she should rely on herself and never forget that he’s a hunter. But then, she goes and does the exact opposite, and she starts the whole thing over again.<br /><blockquote>"The only thing I need to know about him is that his family hunts. I must not forget that. Ever. They kill my kind or sell us to the enkros. In their foul hands, we're either enslaved or butchered. My skin shrinks, and I remind myself he is part of that dark world. Even if he helped me escape, I should avoid him." (59)</blockquote><br />Ok, good. That makes sense. Good thinking.<br /><blockquote>I want to sit with him, talk to him, see him, go out with him ... everything. As long as I'm here, anyway. And not just for the sake of my draki. I would have liked Will Rutledge no matter what I was." (98)</blockquote><br />No! What happened to the smarter girl 40 pages back?! You barely know him, he lives a double life killing your race, and the only reason you're attracted to him is probably <i>because</i> you're a draki and he's something ... else. <i>Not</i> in spite of it.<br /><blockquote>"It's the wake-up call I need. I'm a fool to think a hunter is going to save me. Protect me. Keep me alive. I'll find another way. My fist clenches around his note, crumpling it into a ball in my hand. I'll forget about Will. Sever whatever bond I feel with him. Only the decision doesn't make me feel any better. My chest hurts even more." (101)</blockquote><br />Ok, good. We’re back to Jacinda being sensible. Hopefully things will stay like this …<br /><blockquote>"I don't know if Will's back, but I tell myself it shouldn't matter either way. I can't go out with him, can't let myself rely on him. I <i>won't</i>. Big words. I feel like such a fake. Because despite my vow to forget him, I haven't. I remember everything about him. I feel his absence. Like the loss of shaded skies mists, and pulsing earth. He cannot possibly be all that I remember, all that I crave to see again. Even as I know it's wrong. Even as I know that I must avoid him." (106) </blockquote><br />But, but … we were doing so well five pages back! Now she’s back to pining for the boy who is dangerous to both her and her family. Makes sense, doesn’t it?<br /><blockquote>"Unable to speak, I shake my head, crack open my chemistry book, and stare blindly at the page, telling myself that I'm glad he ignored me. I needed this to remember the vow I made to myself to stay away from him." (110) </blockquote><br />Alright, good. She’s thinking clearly again.<br /><blockquote>"I'm aware of the promise I made to myself. The promise to avoid him." (123)</blockquote><br />Whew. Still going strong!<br /><blockquote>"His words echo inside me. <i>You should stay away from me</i>. Something I already know, but sitting in the front seat of his car, I'm not quite succeeding at that. I wish I could. Wish I didn't feel this pull, this constant tug toward him." (128) </blockquote><br />Uh oh, she’s losing it again.<br /><blockquote>"Apparently, our kiss only convinced him that we needed to pursue this thing between us. Except, our kiss told me the opposite. Kissing him told me what I already knew, but had been denying. I can't risk being with him." (133)<br />"At school, I won't talk to him, won't look at him ... and I certainly won't ever <i>touch</i> him again. If it kills me, I'll ignore him and forever keep my distance." (134)</blockquote><br />Alright, she had a momentary lapse, but she’s come back ‘round to the side of the sane again.<br /><blockquote>"For a moment, I'm there again, hunters in fast pursuit. Wet cold hugs my body. Agony lances my wing, tearing the membrane. It took days for that to heal, for the pain to fade. I drag that memory close, hold it tight, determined to remember. Xander is part of that memory. But then, so is Will. Maybe that's something I've let myself forget. I shouldn't have. I can't. Even with the taste of him still lingering sweetly on my lips, I vow never to forget again." (160)<br />"I can forget him. Turn off everything I'm feeling. I can. I <i>will</i>. He's too dangerous for me to be around. I can do this." (161)</blockquote><br />That idea should be cemented now, right? Ah, but we know how this all ends, it <i>is</i> a teen love story after all.<br /><blockquote>"He looks beautiful standing there, and a familiar ache starts in my chest as I wonder how I can love and fear the sight of someone with the same intensity." (216)</blockquote><br /><b>This whole book is FILLED with this type of back-and-forth shite.</b> “I can’t be near him, I love him, I need to forget him, he’s the only one I can be real around, he hunts my kind and I must never forget, I LOVE HIM…” Ugh, it’s just so annoying. <br /><br /><b>As for the rest of the characters, I didn’t like any of them at all, besides Cassian.</b> Will does some decidedly stalker-ish things to Jacinda which made me like him even less. Both Jacinda’s sister Tamra and their mom are whiny and can’t understand most of what Jacinda is going through; not that it gives Jacinda the right to be just as whiny and even less understanding, but they didn’t make me sympathize with them at all.<br /><br /><b>The mythology of the draki was the book’s strongest selling point, but unfortunately it’s something that feels tacked on rather than the core of the story.</b> I found myself wanting to know more about the draki Jacinda left behind in the pride, as well as Cassian. I really thought she could have expanded on the draki more than focusing on the “love” story between Will and Jacinda. The next book continues Jacinda’s story so maybe I’ll get my wish.<br /><br /><b>This book was such a mess; a sad, sad mess of poorly written teen angst and melodrama, and an obvious example of an author trying to cash in on the genre.</b> Will I read the next one? Yes, because I’m stupid and masochistic, but also because I’m sure my library will get it in. But please, <b>do NOT spend money on this book</b>, it’s just not worth it.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17692226510067834548" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Monisha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13001527-monisha"><img alt="Monisha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1433436407p2/13001527.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/425160773?book_show_action=true">Sep 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Monisha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Monisha" href="/user/show/13001527-monisha">Monisha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13001527-monisha?shelf=high-school-drama">high-school-drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13001527-monisha?shelf=blame-the-cover-for-reading-it">blame-the-cover-for-reading-it</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13001527-monisha?shelf=freaking-love-triangle">freaking-love-triangle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13001527-monisha?shelf=heroine-was-ultra-dumb">heroine-was-ultra-dumb</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13001527-monisha?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13001527-monisha?shelf=rolls-eyes">rolls-eyes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13001527-monisha?shelf=someone-put-me-out-of-misery">someone-put-me-out-of-misery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13001527-monisha?shelf=bangs-my-head-on-the-wall">bangs-my-head-on-the-wall</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13001527-monisha?shelf=dickhead-heroes">dickhead-heroes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13001527-monisha?shelf=goodbye-brain-cells">goodbye-brain-cells</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer425160773" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17561458392366366118"><br/>Shape-shifters are nothing new.<br/>But shape-shifter-dragons? <br/>How cool is that? OR NOT!<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380392889ra/756377.gif' width='300' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I loved the idea, but unfortunately, I <i>struggled</i> a lot with Firelight and story fell short.<br/>There were such high expectations for this book, but it sucked .......BIG TIME!!!!<br/><br/>The tagline for this book is:<br/><br/> →A hidden truth.<br/> →Mortal enemies.<br/> →Doomed love. <----- <i>See, this part was what intrigued me the most!</i><br/><br/>But after a few chapters, this unique story about draki's turned into a <i>"new girl in town meets hot distant boy a</i></span>
  <span id="freeText17561458392366366118" style="display:none"><br>Shape-shifters are nothing new.<br>But shape-shifter-dragons? <br>How cool is that? OR NOT!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380392889ra/756377.gif" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I loved the idea, but unfortunately, I <i>struggled</i> a lot with Firelight and story fell short.<br>There were such high expectations for this book, but it sucked .......BIG TIME!!!!<br><br>The tagline for this book is:<br><br> →A hidden truth.<br> →Mortal enemies.<br> →Doomed love. &lt;----- <i>See, this part was what intrigued me the most!</i><br><br>But after a few chapters, this unique story about draki's turned into a <i>"new girl in town meets hot distant boy at school"</i> story and it lost all uniqueness it had going for it. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380392889ra/756378.gif" width="370" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <u>MAJOR RANT-FEST :</u>
</b><br><br>*********<i>Never say I didn't warn you!!!</i>*******************<br><br>Firelight is much less about dragons than it is about yet another love story between the <i>apparently-average-but-actually-very-special-outsider-girl and the mysterious-has-a-dark-secret-is-her-mortal-enemy-but-is-ultimately-just-a-complete-sweetie-and-love-of-her-live-bad-boy .........</i><br><br>❶ Jacinda is, without a doubt, the worse MC I have read in a looong time.<br>(And, trust me I've read more than my share of infuriating-as-hell MCs.)<br> <br>No! <br>Look at me. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380392889ra/756379.gif" width="250" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>You, Jacinda, are selfish, infuriating, stupid, AND selfish.<br><br>I wanted to strangle her.<br>Whiny little bitch. <br><br><i>'Oh I must do this for my family they must be happy oh no what do I do oh Will is hot hot hot oh no my family OH NO!' </i><br><br>God. Really, I think the author was trying to make the main out as a selfless character. It totally backfired. She just whines about what she think she needs to do, without actually DOING anything.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380392889ra/756380.gif" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>You are worse than Bella Swan, because while she infuriates me as well, I can better tolerate an ridiculous overload of foolish selflessness rather than childish selfishness.<br><br>You.Make.Me.Angry. <br><br>The overall story does that to me, too, but you are really the main reason why I <i>simply stopped caring</i>.<br>(And, let me tell you it's not a good feeling at all!)<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380392889ra/756381.gif" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>She call's her mother, in one fleeting scene... a <b>sadist. </b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/563541.gif" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>You're sixteen, you're angry, I get it. But for a moment, please, just shut up.<br>See, Jacinda is possibly the epitome of adolescent over-reacting. <br><br>By the way, to have more brain cells inside your brain wouldn't hurt, Jacinda.<br><br>WHAT ARE YOU DOING CHANGING INTO A DRAGON AND FLYING OUT IN THE OPEN WHEN YOU KNOW FULLY WELL THERE'RE EVIL DRAGON HUNTERS OUT THERE?????<br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380364589ra/716314.gif" width="250" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>In case you disagree with me, consider this:<br><br>Living in her Draki community, Jacinda feels trapped. Living the the *human* community, Jacinda feels trapped. Living in her Draki community, Jacinda complains of being used. Living with her mom and sister, Jacinda complains about being used. There is no other reason for her mother to make them all leave the Draki community other than Jacinda's safety . If she wanted to leave just for her and Tamra's happiness, wouldn;t they have dragged Jacinda away from her community the instant they learned of her father's death? <br>I'm getting pissed off just remembering it all.<br><span>[image error]</span> <br><br><br>❷Hello, stereotypical high school and teen angst-ridden <s>love</s>(love, love, did I say love??????) story.<br><br>There is lots of standard teenie romance with a special dose of high school drama.<br><br>But my biggest problem is that Firelight is a lust story, not a love story.<br><br>Also, totally did not buy the romance. <br>Sorry, but no. <br>So Jacinda can <b>"sense"</b> Will. <br><br> <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380392889ra/756383.gif" width="300" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Big whoopdee-doo, and I mean crap, we're only told this like five bazillion times, that she lights up like a Christmas tree and starts hyperventilating whenever Will is within a five mile radius. Wonderful. <br><i>Is this supposed to make me believe they're in love? </i><br>Because um... it doesn't.<br>There is no relationship developed between Will and Jacinda. <br>Why do they even like each other? <br><br>They're both hot.(OH, wow, no prizes for guessing!)<br><br>They never talk, and when they do it's very brief, yet we're supposed to believe Will is in love with Jacinda and that Jacinda loves him<i> oh so deeply</i> she'd do anything for him. <br><br>They spend more time making out than getting to know each other. <br><br>As to the male lead Will, I would have been okay with him <br><b>*major plot spoiler warning*</b> <i>if only he didn't turn out to be a freaking stalker.</i><b>*end of spoiler*</b><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380392889ra/756384.gif" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><u>
  <b>Twilight-esque Dialogue</b>
</u><br><br>(Even the name <i>Firelight</i> resembles <i>Twilight</i>, hah!!!)<br><br>Basically half of the novel Will tries to convince Jacinda he and his family are dangerous and she should stay away. <br><br>Later on, Will completely makes a 180 and shows up at her house saying he's tired of trying to stay away from her.<br><br><br>I want to see why the characters fall for each other and I love to see how they fall for each other. <br>Will and Jacinda are just two teens <b>in lust</b> with one another.<br>I don't want to read about a <i>whiny</i> dragon-- I want to read about a fiercely awesome, fire-breathing, scare-the-pants-off-you, courageous, warrior-princess dragon!<br><br>Sigh... I know, I demand way too much from my books.<br><br><br>❸Seriously? <br>If I read ONE MORE BOOK with <i>The Blond Bratty Cheerleader</i> who becomes oh-so-jealous because <i>The Unattainable Guy</i> is head-over-heels for the "Flawed Female Protagonist" because they are "inexplicable drawn to each other"-- I. Am. Going. To. Snap.<br><br><i>Seriously.</i><br><br>❹Oh, and there's a love triangle. 'nuff said.<br><br><br>I can stop right here, because anyone, I repeat, ANYONE can practically spell out the rest of the story from this point.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380352833ra/706218.gif" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>PS:</b> If you can handle cliches flying from all directions, then you might be okay with this book.<br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="17561458392366366118" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_127782729" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/127782729" />
    <a title="Haleema" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4336293-haleema"><img alt="Haleema" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1402430795p2/4336293.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/127782729?book_show_action=true">Oct 24, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Haleema" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Haleema" href="/user/show/4336293-haleema">Haleema</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4336293-haleema?shelf=cheese">cheese</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4336293-haleema?shelf=not-again">not-again</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4336293-haleema?shelf=hate">hate</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4336293-haleema?shelf=pretentious">pretentious</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4336293-haleema?shelf=stupid">stupid</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4336293-haleema?shelf=predictable">predictable</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer127782729" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12691745787885570219">Beware of spoilers!<br/><br/>I feel so... immoral to give this one two stars. However, it doesn't entirely deserve one star either. I was contemplating quite hard before giving this book two stars. Yeah...<br/><br/>First of all, <i>Firelight</i>? It's a good thing that doesn't sound like <i>Twilight</i> because that would have been really stupid...<br/><br/><i>Firelight</i> was about... *tries to think up words* Ummm... uh... eeeh... ohh... Really. What was it about? *ding* Oh, yeah! <i>Firelight</i> was about a monotonous, pessimistic, idiotic, depres</span>
  <span id="freeText12691745787885570219" style="display:none">Beware of spoilers!<br><br>I feel so... immoral to give this one two stars. However, it doesn't entirely deserve one star either. I was contemplating quite hard before giving this book two stars. Yeah...<br><br>First of all, <i>Firelight</i>? It's a good thing that doesn't sound like <i>Twilight</i> because that would have been really stupid...<br><br><i>Firelight</i> was about... *tries to think up words* Ummm... uh... eeeh... ohh... Really. What was it about? *ding* Oh, yeah! <i>Firelight</i> was about a monotonous, pessimistic, idiotic, depressing little twit named <s>Bella Swan</s> Jacinda Jones. She's a fire-breathing dragon, Whoops! I meant <i>draki</i>. That's it. I mean, there wasn't really a praise-worthy plot. Come on. She falls in love with the wrong boy. She has to go back to her own kind. Blah, blah, blah. Whatever.<br><br><b>The characters:</b><br>Jacinda was a clone of Bella Swan. How, you ask? Hmm... let's see.<br><br>1. Pessimistic - I DON'T WANT TO BE HERE! I HATE MY LIFE! EVERYTHING HAS TO BE ABOUT ME! EWW, SCHOOL SPIRIT!<br>2. Monotonous - Girl: YOU'RE ABOUT TO GET BLOWN TO BITS, WOMAN! Jacinda: Don't, please.<br>3. Insanely dependent on a guy who stalks her<br>4. Idiotic<br><br>This girl is the epitome of nothingness. She's an astonishing, beautiful, different, rare, fire-breathing Mary Sue of a loser. She's from Planet Loser. Planet Dumbass. Planet I'm-too-stupid-to-live. Planet I'm-a-waste-of-draki-skin-and-fat. You get the point, right? She's a horrible mixture of Nora Grey and Bella Swan. She's so freaking pathetic with her sob story. She's so dependent on Will. She can't seem to grasp the difficulties of life and MOVE THE HELL ON! She needs Will all the time. "Oh, Will. He's the ONLY one who makes me feel alive inside." Oh, shut the hell up, you stupid twit. She's so damn clingy and stupid. She's a poor excuse for a protagonist. <br><br>- Will Rutchelgodfodjfkdfkdjf. Whatever his stupid last name was. Guess who he reminded me of? Just take a wild, wild guess.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380340780i/697102._SY540_.jpg" width="300" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Except he's not a 107-year-old virgin!<br><br>Will and his oh-so-velvety voice stole the heart of Jacinda. Thank God Jordan didn't mention that Will had a fruity smell to his chest. I would have gone nuts. Will is the perfect Edward Cullen.<br><br>1. He creepily watches Jacinda from a distance through a window without her knowing. Oh, and Jacinda doesn't mind... AT ALL. In fact, she welcomes it. Splendid.<br>2. He saves her from stupid accidents.<br>3. He's the lion and she's the prey.<br>4. Velvetty voice, beautiful face, chiseled body, Gary Stu.<br><br><br><b>The plot:</b><br><i>What plot?</i> Please. Girl has to leave her home. She hates her new home. She falls in love with a stalker. Stalker is her hunter. She has to go back to her home. The end.<br><br>Oh, and I forgot to mention how much of a horny, immoral couple this was. Jacinda and Will. They're the type of people that make Aphrodite and Erik from <i>House of Night</i> look like saints.<br><br>Okay, maybe not <i>that</i> horny, but they made out in a horrid room filled with dead draki skin. Jacinda's people. And Jacinda mentioned that her FATHER might have been in there. Splendid, right? <br><br><b>The writing:</b><br>I couldn't decide whether it was good or not, but now I can. It was horrible! Yes. Jordan took purple prose to a whole new damn level. It's like, "I need to have awesome description so I'm going to go completely overboard with adjectives and adverbs." Holy crap. It was too dense for my taste. Her sentences were extremely choppy and abrupt. They contained so many commas. Jordan is definitely a Commanist.<br><br>- "My lips, dry and charred, touched his, cool and soft. Delicious. I let myself melt into him, feeling his warmth and dying to get more of it, enveloping my arms around his hard waist. Hard, smooth waist."<br><br>Oh, and how many freaking times can a girl lick her lips?<br><br>"I licked my lips. I wet my lips. I ran my tongue across my lips." I seriously read that every two sentences. <br><br>- And this is one of the weirdest sentences I've ever heard: "A feather muscled in his jaw." Or "A muscle feathered in his jaw." Not sure, but it sounded just terrible.<br><br>- And this...<br><br>"The wind kissed my skin."<br>"The water hugged my body."<br>"I drank the air in."<br><br>That just sounds weird and wrong.<br><br><b>Why I gave it two starts:</b><br>Dragons! I love them. I haven't read about them since I finished the <i>Harry Potter</i> series years ago. I found the concept of the draki slightly interesting. I thought the story could have been tons better if it wasn't for the insane resemblance to <i>Twilight</i>. I felt like Jordan had a tiny idea forming in her heard, but she just couldn't get the execution right.<br><br>Overall, <i>Firelight</i> was just a bad, bad, BAD case of <i>Twilight</i> meets <i>Romeo and Juliet</i>. R&amp;J because of the whole "I-can't-love-you-I'm-supposed-to-hate-you" bullcrap. Jordan's romance ruined the whole book. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12691745787885570219" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_134502559" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/134502559" />
    <a title="Lora" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4632071-lora"><img alt="Lora" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1305237530p2/4632071.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/134502559?book_show_action=true">Dec 10, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lora" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lora" href="/user/show/4632071-lora">Lora</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">fans of YA paranormal novels</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4632071-lora?shelf=g-ya-paranorm">g-ya-paranorm</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4632071-lora?shelf=fluffier-than-my-birman-cat">fluffier-than-my-birman-cat</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer134502559" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8885158559771673235">First off, let's start with the things I liked about <i>Firelight</i>:<br/><br/>The writing. Fairly good. Although maybe a little too easy for my taste (I think the biggest word she used was <i>confidante</i>), it had a nice flow that made it easy to flip pages at rapid-fire speed. Also, I thought that the world she created was slightly more original than other paranormal worlds out there right now. I liked the whole "draki" idea, it made for a fresh plot that was more engrossing than most copycat (*cough*vampires*coug</span>
  <span id="freeText8885158559771673235" style="display:none">First off, let's start with the things I liked about <i>Firelight</i>:<br /><br />The writing. Fairly good. Although maybe a little too easy for my taste (I think the biggest word she used was <i>confidante</i>), it had a nice flow that made it easy to flip pages at rapid-fire speed. Also, I thought that the world she created was slightly more original than other paranormal worlds out there right now. I liked the whole "draki" idea, it made for a fresh plot that was more engrossing than most copycat (*cough*vampires*cough*) ideas being published today.<br /><br />The romance: Team Will or Team Cassian? To be honest, I didn't much care for either. Will definitely had his shining moments, but they were few and far between and I felt that he fell flat as far as memorable male characters go; I don't see myself remembering him even next month. And as for Cassian - to be quite honest - he just wasn't in the novel enough for me to really get to know him in order to properly gauge him as a character. Although I will say that in the small glimpses we do see of his character, I found him to be more intriguing than Will.<br /><br />The main character, Jacinda: At first I liked her voice on the page. But then she started to seem a little bit irritating. Mainly because throughout the novel she goes back and forth between wanting to be with Will and thinking that she must stay away from him; I lost track of how many times she did this. That hackneyed plot line (along with the love triangle) just doesn't work for me anymore. <br />I think the only thing I ended up liking about her character was that I could empathize with her and the situation that she was put in because of her mother.<br /><br />I found Jacinda's sister, Tamra, to be very annoying and I just wish she could have been a little more supporting of her sister. I've never liked vain characters.<br /><br />Since I've basically mixed in the good with the bad I'll just finish saying that, all in all, this wasn't horrible, it just didn't live up to my expectations. And as for the sequel, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/9436632.Vanish__Firelight___2_" title="Vanish (Firelight, #2) by Sophie Jordan" rel="nofollow noopener">Vanish</a> . . . it's safe to say that I won't be reading it.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8885158559771673235" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_568667811" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/568667811" />
    <a title="Mizuki" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16842102-mizuki"><img alt="Mizuki" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1368277474p2/16842102.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/568667811?book_show_action=true">Mar 23, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mizuki" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mizuki" href="/user/show/16842102-mizuki">Mizuki</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=unable-to-suppress-my-disbelief">unable-to-suppress-my-disbelief</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=i-hate-love-triangle">i-hate-love-triangle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16842102-mizuki?shelf=young-adult-books">young-adult-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer568667811" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10595485020876874191">2.5 stars. If you can handle cliches flying from all directions, then you might be okay with this book.<br/><br/>Firelight, one hell of cliched book it is, to a point that I want to make a cliches check list:<br/><br/>(1) A heroine who is so very special, she's also the only one of her kind? Check.<br/>(2) A heroine who is tired of everyone paying extra attention to her, and wants nothing to be ordinary? Check.<br/>(3) Said heroine encounters a hunter boy who's supposed to hunt and kill her, but somehow he doesn't? Check.<br/>(4)</span>
  <span id="freeText10595485020876874191" style="display:none">2.5 stars. If you can handle cliches flying from all directions, then you might be okay with this book.<br /><br />Firelight, one hell of cliched book it is, to a point that I want to make a cliches check list:<br /><br />(1) A heroine who is so very special, she's also the only one of her kind? Check.<br />(2) A heroine who is tired of everyone paying extra attention to her, and wants nothing to be ordinary? Check.<br />(3) Said heroine encounters a hunter boy who's supposed to hunt and kill her, but somehow he doesn't? Check.<br />(4) Meeting said hunter boy again in her new school against all odds? Check.<br />(5) Said boy being a dreamboat who's hotly sought after by every girl in school? Check.<br />(6) Heroine being awkward and a misfit in her new school? Check.<br />(7) Bullying, mean spirited Queen Bee in school, who picks on the heroine because she's jealous of the latter? Check.<br />(8) The hunter boy notices/being attracted by no one but the heroine? Check.<br />(9) Forbidden romance? Check.<br />(10) Aside from the hunter boy, the heroine has another admirer, who has been around ever since their childhood and won't let the girl go? Check.<br />(11) Love/Attraction At First Sight? Check.<br />(12) "You know you shouldn't be with him but you want him anyway" cliche? Check.<br />(13) Everyone seems to want the heroine? Check.<br />(14) "It's so dangerous to be with you, but I want you anyway" cliche? Check.<br />(15) Love triangle? Check.<br /><br />To be honest, Firelight reads like Twilight, a slightly better and more eventful version of Twilight <i>if only S.Meyer actually has the tiniest bit of writing talent to save her life</i>. That's all I can say.<br /><br />I also would have forgiven all the cliches in the book if the main character, Jacinda actually <i>did something</i> and had a mind of her own, making her own decisions and carrying them through instead of just ranting about how suffocating her life was whilst allowing herself to be dragged around whenever the pride, her mom and Cassian took over and ran her life for her. <br /><br />The idea of a girl grew up bearing a huge amount of expectation and pressure,how she dealt with it and found herself, is an interesting one, but throughout the book I remain rather indifferent with Jacinda and what she had gone through.<br /><br />By the way, to have more brain cells inside your brain wouldn't hurt, Jacinda. WHAT ARE YOU DOING CHANGING INTO A DRAGON AND FLYING OUT IN THE OPEN WHEN YOU KNOW FULLY WELL THERE'RE EVIL DRAGON HUNTERS OUT THERE?<br /><br />As to the male lead Will, I would have been okay with him if only <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ he didn't turn out to be a freaking stalker. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Jacinda's mother and twin sister are the supporting characters whom we would see the most frequently, but Jacinda's mom was controlling and cruel, wanting to kill a part of her daughter whilst murmuring <i>"It's for your own good"</i>. The twin sister Tamra turned out to be a whinny and a complainer. I know we're supposed to pity them and see how difficult their lives must be, but these two are just so over-the-top that they are unbearable to read.<br /><br />In fact, the briefly mentioned dragon hunters clan seems to be a lot more interesting than Jacinda and her family adding together. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10595485020876874191" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_178328823" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/178328823" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/178328823?book_show_action=true">Jun 20, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lea" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lea" href="/user/show/5152540-lea">Lea</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5152540-lea?shelf=redheads">redheads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5152540-lea?shelf=had-potential">had-potential</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5152540-lea?shelf=meh">meh</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5152540-lea?shelf=not-what-i-thought-it-would-be">not-what-i-thought-it-would-be</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5152540-lea?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5152540-lea?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5152540-lea?shelf=high-school">high-school</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5152540-lea?shelf=dragons">dragons</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5152540-lea?shelf=high-school-drama-fest">high-school-drama-fest</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5152540-lea?shelf=whining-and-pining">whining-and-pining</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer178328823" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer426849964117633026">Alrighty, so I just finished this book. And I'm wavering between a 2.5 and a 3 star review.<br/><br/>Overall, you know, it wasn't bad. I've read much worse (<i>Fallen</i> series, anyone? Anyone?) The premise of the story is different, which I definitely liked-- I mean, a book about a girl who descends from dragons? That's cool. <br/><br/>But... <br/><br/>I don't know, try as I did, there were just things about this book that left me frustrated. It's not that I didn't <i>like</i> it-- more that I think it had the potential to be a lot bett</span>
  <span id="freeText426849964117633026" style="display:none">Alrighty, so I just finished this book. And I'm wavering between a 2.5 and a 3 star review.<br><br>Overall, you know, it wasn't bad. I've read much worse (<i>Fallen</i> series, anyone? Anyone?) The premise of the story is different, which I definitely liked-- I mean, a book about a girl who descends from dragons? That's cool. <br><br>But... <br><br>I don't know, try as I did, there were just things about this book that left me frustrated. It's not that I didn't <i>like</i> it-- more that I think it had the potential to be a lot better.<br><br>Jacinda is a "draki" -- a descendant of the ancient dragon prides that once roamed the earth. Her kind are now an endangered species, as modern-day hunters capture and kill draki for their valuable skins. One of the draki's main defenses is that they can shape-shift into human form in order to blend into the human world-- however, if anyone ever found out that draki can disguise themselves like this, it will probably mean the end of their race. The best thing they can do is stick together and stay as hidden and isolated as possible...<br><br>Sounds like the start to a kick-ass story, am I right??<br><br>Well don't get your hopes up just yet.<br><br>So the first few pages, I was super excited-- Jacinda and her friend Azure sneak off to transform into glittery, iridescent dragons and fly over lakes and mountains, and I was like, <i>sweet</i>! This is going to be some awesome, high-fantasy adventure, all Lord-of-the-Rings or Brisingr-like with dragons and magic and battles... <br><br>Yeeeeah, not so much. About 5 pages later, Jacinda and her sister Tamra are in a beat-up old car with their mom, escaping from the dragon "Pride" for some small town in Nevada. <br><br>Goodbye, magical world. <br><br>Hello, stereotypical high school and teen angst-ridden love story.<br><br>The biggest problem I had with <i>Firelight</i> was the choice of setting. Like I said, the story starts out in this forest with an enchanted village where the draki live, and it's all nature-y and magical, and I'm all ready for this crazy whirlwind dragon adventure. But then, the story takes this huge, random swing over to some modern-day school near Las Vegas-- and now all of a sudden we're in Been-There-Done-That Territory. <br><br>What???<br><br>I don't <i>get it</i>. Why take such an amazingly unique plot and turn it into the same ol' same ol'?? What happened to the dragon/draki mythology??<br><br>I wouldn't have minded the juxtaposition of the two worlds-- draki and everyday-- but we <i>barely</i> got to see anything about the draki. I am seriously hoping that the next book takes place in the draki world, because honestly, I am <i>not</i> a fan of the overdone, cliche high school drama-fest. <br><br>Sorry, I'm <i>just not</i>. <br><br>(SIDE NOTE: I'm ALSO not a fan of lust and shallow physical attraction being passed off as some deep, meaningful, loving relationship-- but I'll leave that lovely little rant for another day.)<br><br>(SECOND SIDE NOTE: OK, can we please talk logic and geography here for a second? Fact: Jacinda's draki pride is located in the Cascade Mountains. This means she and her family lived somewhere between British Columbia and Northern California. THEN Jacinda's mom moves Jacinda to some high school near Las Vegas, Nevada. OK, now PLEASE TELL ME: How is that Will, the hunter who was after her in the Cascades, happens to go to the EXACT SAME SCHOOL in.... Nevada. What are the odds of this? I'm no mathematician, but there ARE more than say, two high schools, between the Cascades and Las Vegas, right? Seriously, I am not buying this ridiculous coincidence.) <br><br>(THIRD SIDE NOTE: Seriously? If I read ONE MORE BOOK with The Blond Bratty Cheerleader who becomes oh-so-jealous because The Unattainable Guy is head-over-heels for the Flawed Female Protagonist because they are "inexplicable drawn to each other"-- I. Am. Going. To. Snap.)<br><br>(<i>Seriously</i>.)<br><br>So let's talk about Jacinda's love interest, Will. Once again, he's not <i>horrible</i>. He's not Edward Cullen or Daniel Grigori, if you know what I mean. Yes, he's got the whole "I'm-bad-stay-away-from-me" vibe going on, all handsome and irresistibly mysterious, and of course Jacinda can <i>not</i> stay away. Since Will is from one of the hunter families who kill draki for their skins, it was a good conflict to have Jacinda--a draki-- fall in love with him. Overall, I liked Will. (Umm... except the part where he went into Crazy-Stalker-Mode and looked up Jacinda's school records-- to see where she lived-- and then <i>SHOWED UP</i> there-- in the <i>middle of the night</i>-- totally uninvited. Yeah. <i>I know.</i>)<br><br>Jacinda herself was an easy enough character to like-- I just didn't think it made any sense to portray her as a typical, average teenager. I mean, she comes from an ancient line of freaking DRAGONS, right?! I just think she should have had something more mystical and ethereal about her-- more depth and connection to her dragon heritage. She just seemed... boring. And she gets kind of whiny at times. I don't want to read about a <i>whiny</i> dragon-- I want to read about a fiercely awesome, fire-breathing, scare-the-pants-off-you, courageous, warrior-princess dragon!<br><br>Sigh... I know, I demand <i>way</i> too much from my books.<br><br>Basically, I just wish that Jacinda stood out from any other teenage character I've read about and had some backbone, because she's a <i>dragon</i> for crying out loud (wow, have I made that point clear yet?)-- not to mention, she's the only <i>fire-breather</i> dragon to exist in over 400 years! Because of this, I wanted to see her be a little more kick-ass and assertive, and a little less (ugh, here it comes) <i>Mary Sue.</i><br><br>I mean, when I think "dragon," I think: <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380351860i/705423._SX540_.jpg" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>OH HELLZ YEAH. Now THAT'S what I'm talking about! Freaking Brooklyn the Bimbo and her sissy cheerleader cronies would get snuffed out like candles if Jacinda was <i>anything</i> like this bad-ass! XD<br><br>Also, totally did not buy the romance. Sorry, but no. So Jacinda can "sense" Will. Big whoopdee-doo, and I mean crap, we're only told this like <i>five billion times</i>, that she lights up like a Christmas tree and starts hyperventilating whenever Will is within a five mile radius. Wonderful. Is this supposed to make me believe they're in love? Because um... it doesn't. Oh-- and how about the fact that Will and his family HUNT AND KILL Jacinda's species and rip them to pieces for their skins?? Hmmmm... I don't know about you, but I would say that's a <i>wee bit</i> of a turn-off, no? <br><br>Finally, the writing style was not my favorite. It wasn't horrible by any stretch of the imagination, and it was able to tell the story between Jacinda and Will fairly adequately. <br><br>I just don't like when writing. is. choppy.<br><br>And fragmented. <br><br>And breaks up sentences. <br><br>Into phrases. <br><br>Like, every. <br><br>Other. <br><br>Line. <br><br>Know what I mean? It's OK if it's to create a feeling or a mood or to explain the main character's thoughts, but it's just so dang difficult to follow throughout an entire book!<br><br>I will be reading <i>Vanish</i> when it comes out. Because really, I feel like this story has a unique premise and that a lot can still be done with it to make it stand out. I'm really hoping that we find out more about the draki- about Azure, Cassian, Nidia, Severan-- honestly, <i>those</i> are the characters I wanted to be reading about, screw the dumb cheerleaders! How do the draki live? What do they do with the gems? Are there dragon battles between the different prides? Can Will become a draki? Will Jacinda's mom rediscover her inner draki and kick some butt? What exactly are the Enkros? I am <i>dying</i> to know!<br><br>So all in all, this story has captured my interest, despite not <i>quite</i> meeting my expectations so far. I still have hopes that the next book in this series will answer my questions and deliver some of that fantasy and magic I'm looking for!<br><br>~Lea @ <a href="http://lcsadventuresinlibraryland.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener"> LC's Adventures in Libraryland </a></span>
  <a data-text-id="426849964117633026" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer179888572619164164">My favorite thing about this book is the draki world that Sophie created. I feel like she only scratched the surface there and that she has so much more to tell us. What an exciting new series to be able to read! I'm very much looking forward to the second book. Is it wrong to beg another author for an advanced copy because I'm not too proud to beg.<br/></span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/103854166?book_show_action=true">May 22, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nic" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nic" href="/user/show/2813423-nic">Nic</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of Shiver</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2813423-nic?shelf=2010">2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2813423-nic?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2813423-nic?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer103854166" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2969424769919169204"><i>Quiet surrounds us. So thick I can taste it. He sends me a sidelong glance, the gold of his hazel eyes sparking warmth in my chest, igniting a burn I thought was dying.</i><br/><br/>Wow, what a stunning book! Firelight was a beautiful tale of forbidden love, danger and mythical abilities. I had high hopes for this book and it didn’t disappoint. <br/><br/>You can tell Jordan is an experienced writer. The way it flowed, the way it captivated me from the first page, it was just magical. I have so many quotes that I love f</span>
  <span id="freeText2969424769919169204" style="display:none"><i>Quiet surrounds us. So thick I can taste it. He sends me a sidelong glance, the gold of his hazel eyes sparking warmth in my chest, igniting a burn I thought was dying.</i><br /><br />Wow, what a stunning book! Firelight was a beautiful tale of forbidden love, danger and mythical abilities. I had high hopes for this book and it didn’t disappoint. <br /><br />You can tell Jordan is an experienced writer. The way it flowed, the way it captivated me from the first page, it was just magical. I have so many quotes that I love from this book.<br /><br />I adore Jacinda. She showed so much strength while struggling to choose between what’s right for her family and what’s right for her. Will is a crush worthy character. Mysterious, protective and a caring soul. Jacinda and Will definitely have great chemistry. Sparks were flying. Those kissing scenes were gorgeous. I found Cassian to be an interesting character even if we know little about him. It sounds like he will be a major part in the next instalment and hopefully we will get to understand the guy behind the dragon.<br /><br />Okay I did have one minor little complaint but that was more to do with my mood than the actual book. The whole mean girl thing bugged me. I thought Jordan wrote it well but I just wanted one book where the girls in the story got along. I guess that is not realistic unfortunately.<br /><br />Ending of course was a big cliffhanger. I could see it coming about 30 pages before the end and starting screaming oh no! But don’t let that stop you from getting Firelight right now because I thought it was well worth the pain of a cliffhanger. <br /><br />Overall, a breathtaking read that I suggest you pick up next time your at the bookstore.<br /><br />Note: I love the cover! It is even more gorgeous when you have it your hands :)</span>

<div id="review_464898552" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/464898552" />
    <a title="Liz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14811808-liz"><img alt="Liz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585394064p2/14811808.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/464898552?book_show_action=true">Nov 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liz" href="/user/show/14811808-liz">Liz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14811808-liz?shelf=headdesk-not-sorry">headdesk-not-sorry</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14811808-liz?shelf=hate-the-heroine">hate-the-heroine</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer464898552" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14023705978347582583"><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380398983ra/771583.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The problem of such books is just that sometimes the write style or the characters or the combination of both, take all the tension. And the book turns out to be fucking awful. <br/><br/>The idea behind the book is actually intriguing and it makes you long for more, but the execution of this idea leaves a lot to be desired...It could have been much better. <br/>It was not. This is the reason why I gave only 2 stars. Sorry... I wish I could give more. <br/><br/>The write style was sometimes just too long-winded and unrea</span>
  <span id="freeText14023705978347582583" style="display:none"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380398983ra/771583.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The problem of such books is just that sometimes the write style or the characters or the combination of both, take all the tension. And the book turns out to be fucking awful. <br><br>The idea behind the book is actually intriguing and it makes you long for more, but the execution of this idea leaves a lot to be desired...It could have been much better. <br>It was not. This is the reason why I gave only 2 stars. Sorry... I wish I could give more. <br><br>The write style was sometimes just too long-winded and unrealistic. Sometimes Jacinda acted like an adult, a wise woman and then, suddenly without any reasons like a fangirling teenager...And it made me feel<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380398983ra/771584.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Same problem with the other characters. All of them were too much character and not enough personality. I did not like a single one. <br><br>The book didn't magane to capture me. I felt a certain distance to everyone and everything in this book. It is a pity, but true...<br> </span>
  <a data-text-id="14023705978347582583" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
