    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_118909386" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/118909386" />
    <a title="Okapi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3638188-okapi"><img alt="Okapi" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/118909386?book_show_action=true">Aug 27, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Okapi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Okapi" href="/user/show/3638188-okapi">Okapi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Hush, Hush fans</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer118909386" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15642551846908457693">As a fan of dragons, the premise sounded promising - a hiatus from vampires, werewolves and angels while still lingering in the paranormal zone. Curled up in my bed for a couple hours, I read this novel in one sitting, my attention constantly tethered to the rapt and engaging plot. But alas, my eyes uncovered a paltry, watery novel that washed through my mind and caused me to forget about it soon after.<br/><br/>I love the concept of draki, the descendants of dragons, morphing into human, and their custom</span>
  <span id="freeText15642551846908457693" style="display:none">As a fan of dragons, the premise sounded promising - a hiatus from vampires, werewolves and angels while still lingering in the paranormal zone. Curled up in my bed for a couple hours, I read this novel in one sitting, my attention constantly tethered to the rapt and engaging plot. But alas, my eyes uncovered a paltry, watery novel that washed through my mind and caused me to forget about it soon after.<br /><br />I love the concept of draki, the descendants of dragons, morphing into human, and their customs are interesting. However, I wish the author included more draki lore and history, along with their feud with the dragon hunters. For example, Jacinda mentions an "evasive flight maneuvers class", which sounds interesting, and I would like to learn more about. Jacinda barely spends any time with the dragon pride, and the reader merely experiences them through her memories. Reading this book would be a much more enthralling affair if we actually encountered the pride alongside her, gaining background information about drakis and enriching myself, thus making the rest of the novel more enjoyable.<br /><br />The majority of the characters are lifeless and perilously flat. Will, who I've now nicknamed as "the Wallflower", fails to be mysterious and sexy as the author intends. He only snags my attention when Jacinda begins pining and whining over him, and though many other reviews claim their love to be intriguing and captivating, all I see is another paranormal romance that bores me. Their love is unbelievably instantaneous and predictable, lacking any depth. When Jacinda's inner draki flares to life around Will, it is the definition of cheesy, especially since the author reveals no explanation of Jacinda's fascination of this bland child. Many other reviews state their relationship to rival the romance in Twilight, but while I'm not a fan of that book, at least the author explains Bella and Edward's love. The romance in Firelight flounders to grapple my regard.<br /><br />Jacinda's remarkably selfish twin sister Tamra and mother are extremely irksome and undeveloped. Her mother forfeited her draki spirit and eschews draki culture seemingly without any reason, and her sister complains about the most frivolous things. They aggravate me using their barely there personalities and do nothing more than set up meek obstacles of conflict for Jacinda to jump over. The character redeeming the rest is Jacinda, since she is surprisingly developed compared to the others; during the novel, my liking for her escalates as she demonstrated selfless, unpretentious qualities. She actually tolerates her irritating family members. I notice some other reviews chastising Jacinda for being selfish, endlessly complaining about the situation that her mother puts her in. However, I would probably react similarly if somebody hacks away part of my soul, just as Jacinda's mother attempts to rip away her draki. Jordan successfully captures Jacinda's raw anguish and the torture of allowing her draki to die, which is the equivalent of losing part of one's soul. She describes Jacinda's quest to maintain her identity using simple, emotional phrases.<br /><br />"I once saw a show about an amputee who lost his leg and still feels it. He actually wakes up at night to scratch his leg as if it's still there, attached to him. They call it a phantom limb.<br />I would be like that. A phantom draki, tormented with the memory of what I once was."- page 37<br /><br />The author's writing is very bland and repetitive, and after a while, I began to tire of Jacinda's distressed musings and cravings for Will. Jordan tends to echo Jacinda's thoughts in an annoying manner, and all her sentences are short and choppy, structured too simply. Though constructed using prose that lacks description, this book still consistently maintains its hooking attribute.<br /><br />The ending is so annoying abrupt and unsatisfying that I couldn't help but roll my eyes once I was finished, asking myself if somebody had pruned off the real end of the manuscript. Don't get me wrong, I always bask in the afterglow of anticipation after reading a superb cliffhanger, but Firelight left off without any conclusion or thoughts to hold onto whatsoever. When I read a cliffhanger, I run off a cliff, though there are always questions and unsolved mysteries that keep me dangling on the edge. Firelight, however, has nothing sparking further curiosity, so I gallop over the edge and plummet to the ground.<br /><br />Overall, this typical paranormal romance ensnared my attention for most of its three hundred pages, causing me to dub it as 'mildly addicting' and file it away at the very back of my mind. I'm sure, like many other paranormal romances, it'll acquire a teen fandom when it releases in September, 2010. I'll probably skim the sequel just to see what's in store for Jacinda and company, but I hold very little hope that this series can possibly redeem itself after this slight disaster.<br /><br />Cover: 2/5 - I'm usually partial to people on covers, and this one's no exception. I dislike how up-close the girl is, and the artificial shade of her hair. However, the golden scales add a mysterious touch.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15642551846908457693" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_111413422" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/111413422" />
    <a title="Carolina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3690652-carolina"><img alt="Carolina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1357772621p2/3690652.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/111413422?book_show_action=true">Jul 13, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carolina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carolina" href="/user/show/3690652-carolina">Carolina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer111413422" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4717350096244523510">Whoever designed this cover was a genius. I loved that this girl actually had a head and a (mostly) visible face. I get worn out with all the headless covers in YA. Still, you have no idea what this book is about because you can't see the body, but one glimpse at this (mostly) human face--the bright red hair, the glitter and the shine and the subtle scales--and you know that somewhere in there, there's some sparkly fantasy. I saw this cover and drooled just a little bit. It was enough for me to </span>
  <span id="freeText4717350096244523510" style="display:none">Whoever designed this cover was a genius. I loved that this girl actually had a head and a (mostly) visible face. I get worn out with all the headless covers in YA. Still, you have no idea what this book is about because you can't see the body, but one glimpse at this (mostly) human face--the bright red hair, the glitter and the shine and the subtle scales--and you know that somewhere in there, there's some sparkly fantasy. I saw this cover and drooled just a little bit. It was enough for me to start coveting like a sinner.<br /><br />I couldn't wait to dive into this book, and from page one, I was hooked. I mean, come on, a humanoid descendant of dragons saved by the dude who hunts her kind? Love it. Hunter falls for his prey? Okay, so I definitely got some TWILIGHT vibes there. So yes, TWILIGHT fans will probably like this book.<br /><br />(You know there's a giant BUT, right?)<br /><br />BUT, while FIRELIGHT has the whole lion-falls-for-the-lamb bit going for it (a premise I think is brilliant, by the way), that's pretty much where the similarities end. For one thing, the female mc is the supernatural being, and a dragon-like shapeshifter at that. She has a special ability, too, and this ability creates a major conflict for her. Yet Jacinda has to deal with major responsibility, including the welfare of her mother and sister, so her own suffering has to be suppressed.<br /><br />Overshadowing everything, however, is the romance with Will, which is just. so. dreamy....the lovers who have every reason to hate one another, but find themselves pulled to be together anyway--and yet their unchangeable identities make it impossible to be together. So Romeo and Juliet, no?<br /><br />I loved the way the story played out. I can't say that I didn't suspect Jacinda and Will would fall for one another (eh hmmm, it IS a romance), but I did NOT see that end coming. Still, you'll want to read it for more than the end. I was captivated by the original handling of mythological concepts, the premise, the lively main characters, the interweaving of the paranormal and the reality-based setting, and the witty, genuine-feeling dialogue. I was sucked in from the start.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4717350096244523510" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer12154248319547112930"><b>*3.5 FIRE-BREATHING STARS*</b><br/><br/><b>
  <i>“What good is safety if you're dead inside?”</i>
</b><br/><br/>Yeah, this book wasn't really my thing, I kind of expected more from it.<br/>I loved the whole <i>draki</i> concept but I wish Sophie Jordan executed it a little better. As you all know, I absolutely hate <i>insta-love</i> and that's exactly what happens here. They meet one minute, they have an instant connection and <b>POOF</b>, butterlies fly and they're madly in love. <b>No, just no.</b></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_119734971" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/119734971" />
    <a title="Jessica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3283298-jessica"><img alt="Jessica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1572125481p2/3283298.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/119734971?book_show_action=true">Sep 02, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica" href="/user/show/3283298-jessica">Jessica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer119734971" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4897320772289173798">Itsy bitsy tiny spoilers ahead!<br/><br/>I don’t know what it is with this book but I’m having an extremely hard time reviewing it.<br/><br/>Maybe I can’t come up with anything to say about it because it’s just like every other paranormal YA novel out there right now? Granted, the whole draki idea is new but they’re basically described to be just like werewolves. Living in a pack with hierarchic structure which is lead by an alpha, displaying an extremely territorial behavior...yada yada yada...Ring a bell? Anyhow,</span>
  <span id="freeText4897320772289173798" style="display:none">Itsy bitsy tiny spoilers ahead!<br /><br />I don’t know what it is with this book but I’m having an extremely hard time reviewing it.<br /><br />Maybe I can’t come up with anything to say about it because it’s just like every other paranormal YA novel out there right now? Granted, the whole draki idea is new but they’re basically described to be just like werewolves. Living in a pack with hierarchic structure which is lead by an alpha, displaying an extremely territorial behavior...yada yada yada...Ring a bell? Anyhow, “Firelight” is definitely one of the better YA novels out there, I really enjoyed it and I was sucked into the story right from page one (which is definitely a plus).<br /><br />I have to say that there were an awful lot of things which reminded me of Nightshade, and I can’t help but compare the two books. (don’t know and don’t care which one was published first, I like Firelight better than Nighshade)<br /><br />Both Calla and Jacinda are supposed to become alphas (or at least the alpha’s wives) someday, meaning they are both already promised. Both of them fall in love with a human who, in the end, turns out to be not so human after all - yay, surprise! (I know, there are some differences but I’m just talking about the basic idea here). In both books we’ve got a love triangle between our heroine, the boy she’s promised to (who’s a jerk in both books) and the human (who’s a crybaby only in Nightshade, thank God). For what it’s worth, I liked the love triangle much better in Firelight than in Nightshade, probably because it was not that much of a triangle to begin with, seeing as our heroine doesn’t really like the guy she’s promised to and we don’t have that forbidden fruit vibe going on.<br /><br />Both books start with the first meeting of our heroine and the human boy in a life-and-death situation. Calla saves Shay’s life, Will saves Jacinda’s – and that’s also where their instant, soul deep connection originates from. *mega sigh and eye-roll* Yeah sure, what else? Even though I’m very sick of these kind of relationships, I didn’t mind it as much in Firelight as I did in Nightshade. Don’t ask me why. I just liked Will a hell of a lot better than Shay. *coughs* Wiener! *chough cough*<br /><br />Um yeah...that’s all I’ve got to say. I really liked Firelight but I don’t feel like elaborating further. Oh, one more thing. I have to agree with Nic, I’m also fed up with the mean girl routine and we’ve got an especially mean specimen in this book.<br /><br />PS: While reading, I counted how many times Jacinda’s “skin tightened”. I don’t know why but I was bothered by the extensive use of that description.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4897320772289173798" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_107028822" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/107028822" />
    <a title="Katieb (MundieMoms)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/470067-katieb-mundiemoms"><img alt="Katieb (MundieMoms)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1286569831p2/470067.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/107028822?book_show_action=true">Jun 14, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katieb (MundieMoms)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katieb (MundieMoms)" href="/user/show/470067-katieb-mundiemoms">Katieb (MundieMoms)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/470067-katieb-mundiemoms?shelf=books-i-own">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/470067-katieb-mundiemoms?shelf=signed">signed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/470067-katieb-mundiemoms?shelf=arcs-i-own">arcs-i-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/470067-katieb-mundiemoms?shelf=2010-100-book-challenge">2010-100-book-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/470067-katieb-mundiemoms?shelf=mundie-moms-review">mundie-moms-review</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer107028822" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17906245029435937621">The back of the ARC describes Firelight perfectly, "Mythical powers and irresistible passion ignite" to make Firelight one book that I was so enraptured with, I read it in one sitting. I've always been intrigued with the mythology of dragons, but I haven't read a book that made me really fall in love with them until I read Firelight. Sophie's characters and her world building hooked from page one and left me wishing her sequel was already out.<br/><br/>Firelight introduces a whole new character in the par</span>
  <span id="freeText17906245029435937621" style="display:none">The back of the ARC describes Firelight perfectly, "Mythical powers and irresistible passion ignite" to make Firelight one book that I was so enraptured with, I read it in one sitting. I've always been intrigued with the mythology of dragons, but I haven't read a book that made me really fall in love with them until I read Firelight. Sophie's characters and her world building hooked from page one and left me wishing her sequel was already out.<br /><br />Firelight introduces a whole new character in the paranormal world- a Draki. Draki's are descendants of dragons who can shift between both dragon and human forms. While the pride closely guards their secret and where they live, they can easily blend in with humans and no one would know it.<br /><br />Jacinda's rare gift of fire breathing makes her a unique Draki who's excepted to be with Cassian, the brooding, hot, Draki Prince whom she was once close to. Now that she's closely watched by her pride, and doesn't have a say in her future, she yearns for freedom. Wanting to get away, Jacinda goes against the pride's rule and flies during the day. This not only puts her in warms way when Draki hunters spot her, but she endangers the whole pride. She also wouldn't have met the Draki hunter Will, who finds Jacinda's Draki just as fascinating as Jacinda finds him. What's even more surprising, is that Will protects her from the other hunters.<br /><br />Jacinda's already lost her father. In order to protect Jacinda and not lose her to the Draki world as well, Jacinda's mom flees from the pride with Jacinda and her sister 13 yr Tamra. Living amongst human's isn't easy for a Draki and living with a mom and sister who can't under Jacinda's Draki needs is even harder. Jacinda struggles with her new life, finds herself at a new school and face to face with the hot Draki hunter Will.<br /><br />Sophie's talent for writing romance makes for some amazingly hot chemistry between Jacinda, Cassian and Will. Will and Jacinda have an undeniable attraction that left the pages of Firelight smoldering. It's not only one of danger as she's a Draki and he's a Hunter, but there's something more to it. I was really drawn to it. That isn't to say there's no attraction with Cassian, but Jacinda fights it. She doesn't want to be with someone who she thinks rule over her. She yearns for her freedom and wants to be loved for who she is, and not what she can do. Personally, I think there's more to Cassian than how Jacinda portrays him. I'm really looking forward to seeing more of them together in the sequel.<br /><br />With it's hot chemistry, a captivating world, and an amazing dragon mythology, Firelight is one book I'll be reading over again. If you're looking for a fresh paranormal book to read, I highly recommend picking up Firelight it releases September 7th.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17906245029435937621" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/95042916" />
    <a title="Kogiopsis" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1462364-kogiopsis"><img alt="Kogiopsis" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1494267218p2/1462364.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/95042916?book_show_action=true">Mar 21, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kogiopsis" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kogiopsis" href="/user/show/1462364-kogiopsis">Kogiopsis</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">FANS OF REALLY SHITTY ENDINGS.  IF THERE ARE ANY.  WHICH THERE AREN'T.</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1462364-kogiopsis?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1462364-kogiopsis?shelf=galleys">galleys</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1462364-kogiopsis?shelf=incoherent-anger">incoherent-anger</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer95042916" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer954550589614443676">(Now with extra British swearing at the end!)<br/><br/><br/>When I say that I just finished this book, I want you to understand- it's been about three minutes. <br/>This does not mean that this book is OMGZ amazing. This is a measure of how righteously OUTRAGED I was at the ending of it.<br/><br/>I cannot even believe that anyone would think to write a book that goes doo, doo, doo, story story story EXCITEMEN- FULL STOP, sorry guys, better pre-order the sequel now.<br/>Eff you, Sophie Jordan. That wasn't even at a lull in the act</span>
  <span id="freeText954550589614443676" style="display:none">(Now with extra British swearing at the end!)<br /><br /><br />When I say that I just finished this book, I want you to understand- it's been about three minutes. <br />This does not mean that this book is OMGZ amazing. This is a measure of how righteously OUTRAGED I was at the ending of it.<br /><br />I cannot even believe that anyone would think to write a book that goes doo, doo, doo, story story story EXCITEMEN- FULL STOP, sorry guys, better pre-order the sequel now.<br />Eff you, Sophie Jordan. That wasn't even at a lull in the action, or a point where the next book will start out with a literal bang (see: Bruce Coville's Dark Whispers. Now, there's a cliffhanger.) This was the most completely illogical place to end a book I could imagine. Compounded, somewhat, by the fact that Jacinda (who I rather liked for a while) suddenly lost all of her brain cells and <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ MANIFESTED IN FRONT OF A GORRAM HUNTER AND THEN NEGLECTED TO TELL THE FUTURE LEADER OF HER PRIDE THAT SHE JUST REVEALED A SECRET THAT WILL DOOM HER ENTIRE RACE. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /> <br />Dammit, I wanted to love this book. DRAGONS. Shapeshifting freaking DRAGONS. FFFFFFFDRAGOOOOOONS. (I love dragons. LOVE 'EM. Have at times wished I was one.) Thankfully, Sophie Jordan is not capable of ruining my favorite mythological creature for me. Not even Todd McCaffrey's horrible, nightmare-inducing attempt to distort his mother's Pern series can ruin dragons. ('Cause I've still got Toothless, and Norbert, and Ramoth, and Skysong, and... you get the picture.)<br /><br />What Jordan did do is ruin her own book for me.<br />I am still so pissed at this I can hardly- nope, I can't. No words.<br />Well, profanity.<br />But I won't share that here.<br /><br />All I have to say is: Dear Sophie Jordan, I will never read one of your books again. You write better than Becca Fitzpatrick or Stephenie Meyer, but that won't absolve you. And unlike Rachel Caine, I haven't read something of yours that I actually like. So we're done.<br />And now I get to go write a scathing galley review for my library.<br /><br /><br /><br />OHYEAH. The second star is for the dragons. Have I mentioned how dragons are the shit?<br /><br />Edit: Here, I found a way to express the profanity properly. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ <a href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=0B4iifg_-b4" rel="nofollow noopener">Colin Firth</a> in The King's Speech. Multiply this by ten and you have my approximate reaction to this stupid book. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="☼♎ Carmen the Bootyshaker Temptress ☼♎" class="user" itemprop="url" name="☼♎ Carmen the Bootyshaker Temptress ☼♎" href="/user/show/16935457-carmen-the-bootyshaker-temptress">☼♎ Carmen the Bootyshaker Temptress ☼♎</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/8710049-firelight">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16935457-carmen-the-bootyshaker-temptress?shelf=exploration-of-middle-earth-orcs">exploration-of-middle-earth-orcs</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer732866138" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2743302343042302516"><strong>Great start to this series.</strong><br/><br/>Right from the start it kept my interest. Secrets will always come out but to try and protect those you love only to find out that there are more secrets. Jacinda has so much she wants but with the only family she has and the rules of her kind it's a tough thing for a young girl. Jacinda has a lot to learn and so much is about to begin for her. <br/>I can't wait to see what is going to happen in the next book. So I'll be making sure I start it soon. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_271320516" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/271320516" />
    <a title="Jacob Proffitt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1331641-jacob-proffitt"><img alt="Jacob Proffitt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1325699498p2/1331641.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/271320516?book_show_action=true">Feb 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jacob Proffitt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jacob Proffitt" href="/user/show/1331641-jacob-proffitt">Jacob Proffitt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Audible Audio " href="/book/show/10230461-firelight">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1331641-jacob-proffitt?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1331641-jacob-proffitt?shelf=unfinished">unfinished</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1331641-jacob-proffitt?shelf=will-probably-regret">will-probably-regret</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1331641-jacob-proffitt?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1331641-jacob-proffitt?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer271320516" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4569833424135549387">This book is full to the brim with stupid. Now, some of that I expected because it's clearly a YA angst novel. Jacinda is exactly the angsty teen Mary Sue you'd expect from the setup. All the hot, socially alpha boys love her but her life isn't <em>that</em> keen because all the girls hate her. Also, everybody is picking on her (except the hot boys she actually likes). Yadda yadda. Like I said, I knew that going in, so that wasn't the problem.<br/><br/>The problem is that <em>everybody</em> in the novel is stupid. Let me i</span>
  <span id="freeText4569833424135549387" style="display:none">This book is full to the brim with stupid. Now, some of that I expected because it's clearly a YA angst novel. Jacinda is exactly the angsty teen Mary Sue you'd expect from the setup. All the hot, socially alpha boys love her but her life isn't <em>that</em> keen because all the girls hate her. Also, everybody is picking on her (except the hot boys she actually likes). Yadda yadda. Like I said, I knew that going in, so that wasn't the problem.<br /><br />The problem is that <em>everybody</em> in the novel is stupid. Let me illustrate: in one scene, Jacinda and a friend are confronted in the girls room by four of the cheerleader/popular squad. Words are said. Eventually, the claws come out and the confrontation becomes physical. The principal suspends <em>Jacinda</em> for <em>bullying</em>. That's right. In this world, a principal is so un-utterably stupid that he'd actually believe that four popular girls were being bullied by two outcasts, one of which was completely new to the school.<br /><br />And don't get me started on her mom. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Jacinda's mom is actively, explicitly <em>trying</em> to "kill" Jacinda's "draki"--her self that turns into a dragon--by moving to the desert where the environment will work to kill it off eventually (apparently irrevocably). That's right, an intrinsic part of her daughter, the part that loves to fly and can do wonderful things, needs to go in a painful and tortuous process that takes months of pain and suffering. Why? Because the pride they used to live in might want to clip her wings (to "tame" her recklessness). So apparently, <em>killing</em> the dragon is preferable to mutilating it? Nobody thinks to call her on this. Nobody. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />So stupid, irrational mom. Stupid, irrational school officials. And stupid, irrational protagonist (which is the only one I expected having to put up with). Add in stupid, irrational everybody else (from her sister to the cheerettes to the love interest, Will), and you have enough stupid that I simply couldn't choke it down any longer.<br /><br />The book is otherwise competently-enough written. Jordan has a talent for evocative description and crafts atmosphere marvelously. I wish that talent had been employed in delivering a better story.<br /><br /><strong>A note about Audible</strong>: I really enjoyed the narrator, but she has a quirk that once you notice, you can't <em>not</em> notice. I didn't mind, but it bears calling out. I'm going to spoiler tag it because nobody should have this inflicted on themselves without me being able to say "told you so" afterwards. Go <a href="http://www.audible.com/pd/Teens/Firelight-Audiobook/B004DR2CK2/ref=a_search_c4_1_1_srTtl?qid=1386613361&amp;sr=1-1" rel="nofollow noopener">listen to a sample</a> and see if I'm not right. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Plummer's intonation is almost an exact copy of William Shatner's Captain Kirk delivery. The same stuttery speed changes in service of dramatic emphasis. As I said, I didn't mind (I kind of like Shatner's Kirk), but once you notice you can no longer <em>not</em> notice. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>
  <a data-text-id="4569833424135549387" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_107206999" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/107206999" />
    <a title="Kelly Hager" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1436215-kelly-hager"><img alt="Kelly Hager" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1422502668p2/1436215.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/107206999?book_show_action=true">Jun 15, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kelly Hager" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kelly Hager" href="/user/show/1436215-kelly-hager">Kelly Hager</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer107206999" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15855697753056116327">This is the first in a series.<br/><br/>Jacinda is a dragon (or, as her people call it, a draki). Dragons are thought to be mythical (although there are some who know they exist, and who hunt and kill them) but there are still some left. They live in prides and what most people don't know is that dragons can manifest as humans. Doing so for a long period of time can cause the draki part of themselves to wither and die; so can living in a desert climate.<br/><br/>After nearly getting killed by some hunters, Jacinda </span>
  <span id="freeText15855697753056116327" style="display:none">This is the first in a series.<br /><br />Jacinda is a dragon (or, as her people call it, a draki). Dragons are thought to be mythical (although there are some who know they exist, and who hunt and kill them) but there are still some left. They live in prides and what most people don't know is that dragons can manifest as humans. Doing so for a long period of time can cause the draki part of themselves to wither and die; so can living in a desert climate.<br /><br />After nearly getting killed by some hunters, Jacinda and her mom and sister flee the pride to live among humans. Her family is excited for the change (her sister never became fully draki and her mom let that part of herself die after Jacinda's father was killed) but Jacinda's devastated. She was a fire-breather, the first one in generations, so she was special to her clan.<br /><br />And she hates living among humans. Except there's this boy...<br /><br />I really liked Jacinda and this was a unique story. I feel like I've read a lot about vampires and zombies and ghosts and werewolves, but this is the first book I've read in ages about dragons. It makes for a very nice change. I'm excited to read the next book in the series.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="15855697753056116327" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_244797708" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/244797708" />
    <a title="Megan Fermo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5352658-megan-fermo"><img alt="Megan Fermo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1382618709p2/5352658.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/244797708?book_show_action=true">Dec 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Megan Fermo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Megan Fermo" href="/user/show/5352658-megan-fermo">Megan Fermo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">YA addicts who really just want to read and get lost on whatever fantasy as long as it IS fantasy</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Megan by: </span>
      A dear, poor friend. 
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5352658-megan-fermo?shelf=wont-even-try-anymore">wont-even-try-anymore</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5352658-megan-fermo?shelf=bit-disappointing-to-have-read">bit-disappointing-to-have-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer244797708" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15535201489325297795">Spoilers ahead!<br/><br/>We've all been sixteen, haven't we? We've all felt that unexplainable anger boiling inside of us, that resentment, the feeling that no one is the world understands, or cares. I know how it is to wake up in the morning only to fall back in bed, because you think no one is going to care whether you get up or not anyway. It's only natural. We all go through it. <br/><br/>But we grow up.<br/><br/>Page 45. That's precisely the page where I just stopped caring. I read on, of course, but I didn't truly care</span>
  <span id="freeText15535201489325297795" style="display:none">Spoilers ahead!<br><br>We've all been sixteen, haven't we? We've all felt that unexplainable anger boiling inside of us, that resentment, the feeling that no one is the world understands, or cares. I know how it is to wake up in the morning only to fall back in bed, because you think no one is going to care whether you get up or not anyway. It's only natural. We all go through it. <br><br>But we grow up.<br><br>Page 45. That's precisely the page where I just stopped caring. I read on, of course, but I didn't truly care anymore. Why?<br><br>Jacinda is, without a doubt, the worse MC I have read in a looong time.<br><br><a href="http://photobucket.com/images/rolling%20eyes%20gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380364589ra/716309.gif" alt="Taylor Swift rolling eyes Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>No! Look at me. You, Jacinda, are selfish, infuriating, stupid, and selfish. You are worse than Bella Swan, because while she infuriates me as well, I can better tolerate an ridiculous overload of foolish selflessness rather than childish selfishness. You make me angry. The overall story does that to me, too, but you are really the main reason why I simply stopped caring. <br><br>You're sixteen, you're angry, I get it. But for a moment, please, just shut up. <br><br><a href="http://photobucket.com/images/shut%20up%20gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380364589ra/716310.gif" alt="shut up gif Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I felt like doing that to you a hundred times while reading your story, then I'd be taking you away for some seriously tough lovin'.<br><br><a href="http://photobucket.com/images/discipline%20gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380364589ra/716311.gif" alt="Discipline Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a> <br><br>But lets do some explaining first. We all know that Firelight is a story about dragons <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ <a href="http://photobucket.com/images/dragon%20gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380364589ra/716312.gif" alt="dragon gif Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a>  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> Or, rather, the Draki. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ <a href="http://photobucket.com/images/dragons%20gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380364589ra/716313.gif" alt="Dragon gif. Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a>  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><br>To be fair the culture of the Draki is the most interesting part, their cultish community, the powers and law. If only the author had taken advantage of that strange culture and put it into good use. If only she had thought of a more risk-taking plot to go with her Draki. I have read too many YA fantasy books only to have their intriguing fantasy marred by their dumb plots and blockheaded MCs. Firelight is no different. Instead of Draki fights and politics, instead of real drama and gripping suspense, we once again get....a high school love story. <br><br><a href="http://photobucket.com/images/crying%20gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/275018.gif" alt="Dean crying Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Those tears are not for their Romeo and Juliet wannabe tale. Those tears are for yet another sample of society's dying, wasted talent. I am hurt emotionally, mentally, and physically by this growing fact. I won't kid myself, I do believe that the author has some writing skill(although her dialogues are atrocious) but again its all hidden beneath this shallow MC of hers.<br><br>See, Jacinda is possibly the epitome of adolescent over-reacting. The friend that forced me to read this practically had tears in her eyes <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ <a href="http://photobucket.com/images/crying%20gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/547562.gif" alt="crying hug Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> as she handed me this book. <br><br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">["She's me, Meg! I am Jacinda! God, she really is me." she said.<br><br>"Why?" I asked, truly curious. "How?"<br><br>"Oh, just read it. You'll see." I did see it.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>My friend, you see, is a drama queen. Youngest kid in her family of three.<br><br>Jacinda, as you know, is a drama queen. Most special kid in her family of three.<br><br>I, of course, expect them to get along fine.<br><br>One sunny afternoon Jacinda and her friend leave their cultish community hoping to be able to fly. They're tired of nighttime flights. Jacinda feels trapped in her community, like a trophy of some rot. She no longer feels like Jacinda, the person, rather, she feels like Jacinda, that Fire-breathing Draki, the only one of its kinda of centuries. And, like we all expect, she doesn't like it. She doesn't enjoy being treated this way. (You must remember this for later on).<br><br>It all goes fine for a while, but then hunters began chasing them down. One of them, a hot, warm, HOT guy finally traps her, but oddly enough lets her go. <br><br><a href="http://photobucket.com/images/damn%20gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380364589ra/716314.gif" alt="Damn gif Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>For no reason at all he lets her go. <b>WHY??</b> What was it about that one particular Draki that made you, well, not want to capture it? What was so different about that one Draki? There <b>needs</b> to be a good reason why. If he had caught her then there wouldn't even be a story to tell, and I would be reviewing a better book right now.<br><br>Since I can't change what's done anyway, I'd rather ask you to remember that one guy. <br><br>Flying during daytime is against the rules, so when Jacinda eventually returns to her community, the other Draki's are worried and pissed off. Her mother can tell that they're probably going to discipline Jacinda <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ <a href="http://photobucket.com/images/yey%20gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380364589ra/716315.gif" alt="yey :) Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a>  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> but before they even get a chance, she and her two daughters sneak past the guard and escape punishment. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ <a href="http://photobucket.com/images/pissed%20off%20gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380364589ra/716316.gif" alt="Mickie Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a>  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> This is where I really start hating the MC. <br><br>She has a twin, the only tolerable character is this book, named Tamra. Tamra, unlike her uber special sister, never manifested, and has had to endure being forgotten in their community her whole life. Jacinda said it herself, despite this and the many other hurtful things Tamra has been through, she's never really complained and mostly accepted things they were they were.<br><br>That's strength, Jacinda. You're missing it, you mopey bitch. <br><a href="http://photobucket.com/images/pissed%20off%20gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380364589i/716317.gif" alt="pissed off gif Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I know, I know, her mother <b> is </b> in fairness struggling to destroy a part of Jacinda's soul, her Draki <b> all for the sake of keeping their family safe, *after all* </b> I would be hurt, too, I'd feel betrayed, I'd feel trapped...but then I'd look past all those emotions and apply logic to our situation. I'm sixteen, too, you know, but I'd grow up. <br><br>Jacinda tries never-endingly to make her mother and sister out as demons. As selfish, selfish demons. She tries to paint her sister as a self-interested, stingy, inconsiderate bitch, but it just doesn't work. In fact, the more she tries, the more I feel sympathetic towards Tamra, the poor thing. Jacinda has been the darling, the trophy of their community her whole life. She's a rare fire-breather, Tamra isn't even a Draki. Isn't it her turn to have a little fun? Then with her mother, Jacinda whines about how her mother killed the Draki part in her mostly because of her defunct sister, trying perhaps to show how her mother has always been on her sister's side. I don't think so, I don't think so at all. I think its a mother thing to do, just so Tamra won't feel that lonely anymore. After all, Jacinda had her father, her friends. She's just a self-centered brat. <br><br>In case you disagree with me, consider this: Living in her Draki community, Jacinda feels trapped. Living the the *human* community, Jacinda feels trapped. Living in her Draki community, Jacinda complains of being used. Living with her mom and sister, Jacinda complains about being used. There is no other reason for her mother to make them all leave the Draki community other than <b> Jacinda's safety </b> . If she wanted to leave just for her and Tamra's happiness, wouldn;t they have dragged Jacinda away from her community the instant they learned of her father's death? I'm getting pissed off just remembering it all.<br><br><a href="http://photobucket.com/images/crazy%20gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/424777.gif" alt="Crazy Gif Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>And so what if their actually enjoying their new, normal lives? Would you rather everyone act tortured like you? At least you're mother and sister can see the brighter part of things. Maybe you should try it. <br><br>Some people would say, hey, she's just a teenager. Teenager's tend to take things too dramatically. Again, I'm sixteen, not exactly a mature person, but I would've acted better if i were in her shoes. can understand if my mom is just doing it for my sake. Hell, even after her mom explains about the community's planned punishment for her [they were going to cut off her wings...if only] she still acts as though <b> HER MOTHER </b> is the root of it all. <br><br>She call's her mother, in one fleeting scene... a sadist. <br><br><a href="http://photobucket.com/images/bitch%20gif%20tumblr" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380364589ra/716318.gif" alt="bitch gif tumblr Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>And as much as I hate her selfishness, this plot point <b> really </b> pisses me off. She goes to a normal school acting like a prick, the kind that tries so hard to ruin things for everyone else, along with her enthusiastic sister. She looks for her locker, finds it, and stops. She heats up, she's glowing. Know why?<br><br>She has just seen the same guy, the same hunter, who had let her, as a Draki, go free back in the cave.<br><a href="http://photobucket.com/images/stupidity%20gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380364589ra/716319.gif" alt="stupidity gif Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>I can stop right here, because anyone, everyone, can practically spell out the rest of the story from this point.<br><br></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="15535201489325297795" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_93715240" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/93715240" />
    <a title="~Tina~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2594672-tina"><img alt="~Tina~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411474324p2/2594672.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/93715240?book_show_action=true">Mar 12, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="~Tina~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="~Tina~" href="/user/show/2594672-tina">~Tina~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=read-2010">read-2010</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=cover-crazz">cover-crazz</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2594672-tina?shelf=order-next">order-next</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer93715240" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10428152273825024086"><b>May contain some spoilers</b><br/><br/>(3.5 Stars)<br/><br/>Jacinda is a Draki, who can shape-shift from human to Dragon. Uniquely gifted she is favored and adored amongst her Pride, but inside she's trapped and hates that she has to follow everyone's rules, not having the luxury of wanting anything for herself.<br/>One morning, Jacinda breaks a rule and almost gets caught, almost revealing her people to hunters who seek there skin and bodies for there own gain and the Pride isn't happy about this. <br/>Her mother fears for her </span>
  <span id="freeText10428152273825024086" style="display:none"><b>May contain some spoilers</b><br /><br />(3.5 Stars)<br /><br />Jacinda is a Draki, who can shape-shift from human to Dragon. Uniquely gifted she is favored and adored amongst her Pride, but inside she's trapped and hates that she has to follow everyone's rules, not having the luxury of wanting anything for herself.<br />One morning, Jacinda breaks a rule and almost gets caught, almost revealing her people to hunters who seek there skin and bodies for there own gain and the Pride isn't happy about this. <br />Her mother fears for her safety and takes Jacinda and her twin sister Tamra and flee before anything could happen.<br />The day she walks the halls of her brand new high school, there she sees a boy with honey brown hair, a boy she remembers deep in a cave....<br /><br />Now this is a element I don't find very often in my reads. <br />Dragons. Love them!<br /><br />First off, I gotta say how much I adore Sophie Jordan's gorgeous writing style. It's beautifully done, so much so that it's almost like each sentence is attached to it's own emotion. Very striking, very remarkable, and very easy to get lost in this world through her words.<br /><br />Jacinda is a great character, but I think she's very lost, very confused when she's in human form, but when she's Draki she has a beautiful vibrate confidence that I admire. I like her, but her indecisiveness and inner turmoil where Will is concerned was very frustrating. The constant yo-yo effect of 'I can't be with him' - 'I need to be with him' was very repetitive and I was screaming at her to just make up her mind already! Apart of me understands <i>why</i> she was this way since she could never hope to want anything for her own self, always denied, always following someones else set of rules, deciding her life, her destiny, so it would be hard for her to make a rational choice when it comes to attraction/longing and right and wrong. She's definitely a conflicted creature.<br /><br />Will is a great character. Good heart, mysterious, confident but a mess. He and Jacinda had a few swoon-worthy scenes that I thought was very sweet, but they have an obvious chemistry; The connection, The pull, The attraction. I guess I wish it was based on something more solid. I understand Will's feelings concerning Jacinda more then her feelings actually. Does Jacinda want Will <i>for</i> Will? Or does she want him because he awakens her Draki, because he's her link to the sky? I wasn't ever really clear about that, not even in the end, or maybe I just didn't feel it.<br />Still, the idea of hunter and prey falling in love, forbidden love, is exciting and enticing.<br /><br />The actual storyline is fascinating and I devoured those few chapters at the very beginning, loving this world of high mountains and rich atmosphere, but sadly the story took a different turn and I was a bit disappointed by that. It touches down on some of the lore but I would have loved to see the world, the different Draki's, what Enkros are, hear there legend and learn there myths. I've read high school drama before, I wanted to see what the dragon world would be like.<br />I did however like the relationship between Jacinda and her twin Tamra. There is a lot of resentment and pain with both of there stories, but in the end, they are sisters, and I very much liked that part of the story.<br />I also thought that brooding Cassian (great name) was an interesting character and wish we got to understand him more. At this point, I'm not sure of his intentions but apart of me wants to believe in him. I look forward to reading more about him in the next book.<br /><br />I don't want my review to seem like I'm ranting, cause I really did enjoy and love this book. The lore is brilliant, the plot is captivating and gripping and the characters are amazing and extremely intriguing.<br />The ending of the book has me anticipating the sequel that much more, making <b>Firelight</b> a promising beginning to a series I very much want to devour!<br /><br />A Great Read!</span>
  <a data-text-id="10428152273825024086" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Whitney" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3827678-whitney"><img alt="Whitney" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1580343008p2/3827678.jpg" /></a>

    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/206530693?book_show_action=true">Sep 08, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer8182976697678089914">Dragons. <i>Finally.</i> <br/><br/>I really enjoyed this book. Like...<b>a lot.</b> I was hoping to find/read a YA book that's about dragons. Or in this book's case, <i>draki.</i> Definitely a whole new original unique story. It caught my attention from the first chapter; that's what I like. ;)<br/><br/>The scenery in this has been definitely used in other books. School, then woods. So it wasn't much to call <i>amazing.</i> But it was totally cool, considering it was dealing with dragons descendants. :3<br/><br/>There's only a few characters in this ar</span>
  <span id="freeText8182976697678089914" style="display:none">Dragons. <i>Finally.</i> <br><br>I really enjoyed this book. Like...<b>a lot.</b> I was hoping to find/read a YA book that's about dragons. Or in this book's case, <i>draki.</i> Definitely a whole new original unique story. It caught my attention from the first chapter; that's what I like. ;)<br><br>The scenery in this has been definitely used in other books. School, then woods. So it wasn't much to call <i>amazing.</i> But it was totally cool, considering it was dealing with dragons descendants. :3<br><br>There's only a few characters in this are easy to like <i>for me</i>. As in Jacinda, Will, Catherine, and Cassian. I didn't like Tamra, the mom, Brooklyn, Xander, and Angus. Tamra was waaaaaay too whiny, it seemed like she only thought about herself. (But I kinda feel sorry for her. o.O) And I didn't like Jacinda's and Tamra's mom, just in general. But I understand why she's like that. Protection, safety, yadda yadda. =.= Xander can just go rot in a hole infested with draki. Angus too.<br><br>I really liked Will. &lt;3 He was just so cute and adorable.~ He was totally easy to like. :3 But then there's Cassian. It's my nature to fall for the underdog. &gt;w&lt; He really did seem like he wanted to love Jacinda more than the pride wanted them to mate. It was frustrating, totally. But Cassian is a big hunk of male that seemed swoon worthy. :D<br><span>[image error]</span><br><br>I seriously need the next book. Like. Now. ._. <i>
  <s>I knew I should've gotten it when I got then first. &lt;_&lt;</s>

<div id="review_234081943" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/234081943" />
    <a title="Annie Brewer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5315988-annie-brewer"><img alt="Annie Brewer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1442496062p2/5315988.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

              <span id="reviewTextContainer234081943" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4040381157602644060">AHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHH!!!!!!!!!!!! I'm having the best of luck finding books that captivate me, and this was no exception. And it was so different from the normal YA PNR.<br/><br/>Hot damn! I read this in a day, 24 hours. Shit! I couldn't put it down. I reluctantly did only to sleep and occasionally pay attention to my kids. Otherwise I was sucked, immersed into this magical world and never wanted to leave.<br/>Fucking amazing!<br/>This book was one hell of an amazing journey! I loved every second of it. I love d</span>
  <span id="freeText4040381157602644060" style="display:none">AHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHHH!!!!!!!!!!!! I'm having the best of luck finding books that captivate me, and this was no exception. And it was so different from the normal YA PNR.<br><br>Hot damn! I read this in a day, 24 hours. Shit! I couldn't put it down. I reluctantly did only to sleep and occasionally pay attention to my kids. Otherwise I was sucked, immersed into this magical world and never wanted to leave.<br>Fucking amazing!<br>This book was one hell of an amazing journey! I loved every second of it. I love dragons. They're so amazing, beautiful creatures. It was such a refreshing story from all the other PNR books out there. <br>It was also awesome to have the heroine, Jacinda be the creature, being among humans. Draki. That was fascinating, unique. I loved seeing her manifest into her purple and blue and green skin and her wings. Just amazing!<br><br>Jacinda<br><br><a href="http://s981.photobucket.com/user/goddess793/media/Jacinda_zpse4b2020e.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380362940i/714151.jpg" alt=" photo Jacinda_zpse4b2020e.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Will. I loved him from the start. He was the perfect hero, human and accepting from the get-go of what Jacinda was. But still wanting to be with her. The sexual tension between these two was electrifying, thick. But it was also a connection they shared, deeper than the physical. Will saved her over and over from his family. The people that hunt her kind. He saved her and kept her secret between them. I love this quote from Will, "A hunter in love with his prey." Gah, yes I love you too Will. Fuck, all these heroes named Will. I'm doomed. <br><br>Will Rutledge.....*dreamy sigh*<br><br><a href="http://s981.photobucket.com/user/goddess793/media/Will-Firelight_zpsb21379fc.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380362940i/714152.jpg" alt=" photo Will-Firelight_zpsb21379fc.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>But then shit got real. And it got real. So much was happening, I was pacing with my book in hand, nervous as fuck. I knew something was going down. OMG I was so pissed and scared, especially towards the end. Ugh. No!!! That ending! Damn you Cassian! You fuck face asshole! I hate you!! Go back to the pride and stay there!!! She doesn't love you, you controlling, jealous piece of shit!!!!! Ahhhhhhh!<br><br>Xander, you're an asshole too! I hope Will beats the living shit outta you! This is all your fault!!! And Tamra, you're such an immature selfish brat for hurting your sister!!! I hope you get better in the next book. I'm so pissed right now! I have to go to sleep with that ending on my mind! I'm too tired to start the next one that is sitting on my shelf begging me to pick up. UGH! God, I'm so pissed!!! <br><br><br>Anyway, sorry I got carried away but I'm just so pissed right now. This book was amazeballs, awesomesauce! I loved every second of it!!! Every. Second. Go read it! READ IT!!!! GO!! <br><br><br><br>Jacinda in her Draki form......Beautiful!<br><br><a href="http://s981.photobucket.com/user/goddess793/media/Firelight_zps11984a43.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380362940i/714153.jpg" alt=" photo Firelight_zps11984a43.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('cMj9/RnlMHxE7AlrPhGJ5L9+ACEnWlxeovT6vMDSuGzKQsfQR7hjeGsexWhkczQxIuItk7kXNLy8SmFv/nR97A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('1gr4UTbmh/SGd+RfwEY3Cs6dMPMaa0mEtr6x31tKvtRsgMJ8aLvU8KmFKFyaJIrfUwEdQYQmIWaoACoMZex7VA==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer15628090233114236534">Pseudonym: <br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1046722.Sharie_Kohler' rel='nofollow noopener'>Sharie Kohler</a><br/><br/>Sophie Jordan took her adolescent daydreaming one step further and penned her first historical romance in the back of her high school Spanish class. This passion led her to pursue a degree in English and History.<br/><br/>A brief stint in law school taught her that case law was not nearly as interesting as literature - teaching English seemed the natural recourse. After several years</span>
  <span id="freeText15628090233114236534" style="display:none">Pseudonym: <br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/1046722.Sharie_Kohler" rel="nofollow noopener">Sharie Kohler</a><br /><br />Sophie Jordan took her adolescent daydreaming one step further and penned her first historical romance in the back of her high school Spanish class. This passion led her to pursue a degree in English and History.<br /><br />A brief stint in law school taught her that case law was not nearly as interesting as literature - teaching English seemed the natural recourse. After several years teaching high school students to love <i>Antigone</i>, Sophie resigned with the birth of her first child and decided it was time to pursue the long-held dream of writing.<br /><br />In less than three years, her first book, <i>Once Upon A Wedding Night</i>, a 2006 Romantic Times Reviewers' Choice Nominee for Best First Historical, hit book shelves. Her second novel, <i>Too Wicked To Tame</i>, released in March 2007 with a bang, landing on the USA Today Bestseller's List. </span>
